<Rating>4</Rating><Review>This place is not like what it used to be a year ago. The ownership & management has changed this year and they seem to care less about their residents now. In the last 6 months alone I have visited their office more times than I did in my previous 2 years of stay here. I hope they can get their act together. They are not even as responsive now if you put in a maintenance request. In the last few months, they have entered our unit a few times but they give only 1 day notice for that. Twice we were out of town for a few days and entered in that time. Obviously we had no prior knowledge or notice since they give 1 day notice only. Both times lights were left turned on. We returned in the middle of the night and were worried if the place was broken into.  There was another incident where our water heater stopped working. There was no hot water and it was so painful to have someone come and fix it. It was out for days. We were given a key to another apartment to use for shower. At first, we got the key which did not work. Luckily for us, Freddy (maintenance staff) was around and we found him to let us in. He was also super nice to put shower curtains in the empty unit when I requested him because all water was spilling out from the tub.

Last time, we had overflow leak in the toilet tank in guest bathroom. We didn't even feel like going to the office to submit the request. The problem would stop if we turn off the inlet valve and turn it back on. When I saw Freddy around, I asked him what might the problem be, just casually - I didn't expect anything from him. < Name>
Rob Hoerntlein< /Name>
< time>
1621187505681< /time>
< rating>
4</rating>
< review>
A nice place to visit. The story of how it got to this location is fascinating. Of course it started here in the 1850's.

About a hundred years later a man in the Valley, not far from here was creating a western theme park and wanted to have a historic jail. He had it taken apart brick by brick and moved to his new park.

After he died his heirs wanted to sell the property. The new buyer wanted to use it for something else. He notified the county that if we wanted it back we had to get it quickly or it would be bulldozed.

That isn't something that can be done quickly. They put the word out and put a committee together that began raising the money and talent needed.

The county donated the land. A group of people went, took it apart brick by brick and rebuilt it where it is now. Not very far from where it was 150 years earlier.

I know that I made it sound easy. It wasn't. There were many fundraising problems, several times it seemed like it wouldn't happen. Then the brain power and labor that understood and was willing to defer to the architect and historians. Maybe you're beginning to understand that there are many people to thank for it being here.</review>

<user_id>107912069581893217197</user_id><Name>Chris LeSueur< /Name><date>1533573475176<//date><rating>5</rating>< Text>
Every year my family makes the trek from SoCal to vacation in Shaver Lake and every year I pass by the Chuck Wagon in Sager California wondering what magic resides in this walk-up food shack with the proclamation...Home of the "Chili Dog". This year my wife helped me with this bucket-list item by agreeing to stop at Chuck Wagon for lunch before heading into the Sierras. Was it a good "Chili Dog" you ask? Oh Yes, a very good chili dog...I would highly recommend it if you like Chili Dogs. But, if you do not like chili dogs this will not convert you.  The Chili Cheese Fries are also great, they put lettuce on top...I think that is the Chuck Wagon version of a salad. The star of the show is probably the Frito Pie my wife ordered. What is a Frito Pie you ask?...One small bag of Frito corn chips sliced open sideways, and then add chili, cheese, onions, and lettuce...served with a spork. Delicious!

I love that this place has existed for all these years and just keeps on going. It was obvious that it is popular with locals, not many tourists stopping in. Would I go back? You bet! That being said I don't think it will become a yearly tradition as my wife and daughter were not as thrilled with the Chuck Wagon as myself. But this place put a huge smile on my face and I will surely be back their again some day.<//Text>

<userid>117960634216369547783</userid>< Name>
Elizabeth Steinhauer-Clark< /Name>
<date>1553818084301</date><rating>5<//rating><Text>The Chuck Wagon is a Sanger, CA institution.  As a long, long, long time Sanger resident I may be biased, but I do love this place.  If you have never been there before, it may seem intimidating but the staff is willing to answer questions.  The "Clark Burger" (no affiliation) is your standard double cheeseburger.  The chili is a meat (no beans) chili.  If you like good, greasy chili, then you will like this.  Much better (IMHO) than Tommy's in Southern California.  I know from which I speak on that point, as I went to school in SoCal and spent many a late night at Tommy's.

Fries are crinkle cut and always done to perfection.   I recommend using them to scoop up any chili that has fallen off of or out of your chili dog or Chili Clark.

Best bets? Most anything with chili on it - chili dog, chili cheese fries, chili Clark.  Note that chili cheese fries come with lettuce and onions on them.  I order without those items, but it is a matter of personal preference.

I will forever (or until such time as they get a new shake machine) miss having a chocolate milkshake with my chili dog.< /Text><pics>None<//pics><Resp>None<//Resp>< GmapID>

< review>
Its OK. Everyone from Sanger always swears by it "the best place ever!!!!" My wife and her family are from Sanger and love love LOVE it. But I bust everyone's bubble...I work at a supermarket...and one day at work I was stocking an aisle. And I saw these people near the chili beans. And I overheard "now let's get the stuff for chuck wagon..." And I saw the lady and man grab every can of Hormel chili (no beans) off the shelf...and I was thinking..."I knew it!" Everyone loves the chili...but its straight up can chili...maybe they add an ingredient or 2 but it's just can chili...so there. Hope I didn't crush all of your dreams...< /review>

3< /Rating>
<review>I got a Clark burger plain (just meat and cheese on a bun), wife got a chilli cheese dog with onions, and we split chilli cheese fries without onions. The chilli is sauce and ground beef without beans. The fries are the crinkle cut type.
I thought the chilli has a light taste reminiscent of the taco meat that you get from Taco Bell but the wife disagreed.
Overall the taste of the food isn't going to explode in your mouth. It's plain. The burger was lightly seasoned and I'd say the taste in the meat was mostly from the grill rather than seasoning. I think the key here is to get the chilli sauce on your hot dog or hamburger.  Even if you do get the chilli it's not aggressive, it's not going to make you think it's homemade and it's not going to win any chilli contest. It's also not likely to give you heartburn which is a plus.
Lastly, the chilli cheese fries came out less warm than you would expect. This could be due to the wait time. We went on a Saturday at about 630PM and there was a sizeable line and we waited about 15 minutes to get our order.< /review>< Pics>
None< /Pics>
